### Conclusion

#### Next steps
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Emily] Web forms are the center of all interactions with your customers.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=4)** They provide you with an opportunity to converse with your end users, help them fulfill their tasks, and therefore enable you to connect and to personalize an interaction with your viewers.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=15)** The differences between a great form and a bad one can be almost too subtle to notice or can even be completely counter-intuitive.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=23)** The color of a button, the location of labels, the manner in which the inputs are formatted, the placement of the form itself, you name it, everything seems to have an impact on a form's performance.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=34)** Just remember, content should be relevant.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=38)** The link between what your users just read and what you're asking must be clear.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=42)** Content should be concise.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=44)** No one has time, so making your copy to the point and as clear as possible is key.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=50)** Keep in mind any reason to doubt the purpose of the form or any sort of ambiguity can have a huge impact.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=57)** Only ask for what matters.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=59)** Focus on what you really need.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=61)** Group and simplify.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=63)** Group the different options where possible, and make sure they're organized.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=68)** Use check boxes instead of asking people to type.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=71)** Make it clear what data goes where.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=74)** Validate information as your users type it in.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=76)** It gives them a feeling of confirmation that they're doing things right, and they aren't filling in a form only to realize that they've made a mistake and have to start all over again.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=85)** A form gets a lot of extra attention from your visitors.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=89)** That's why your form should be completely free of errors, and this way the interaction is seamless.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=94)** You don't want to frustrate and alienate your users.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=97)** You want to instill trust.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=99)** Follow the design tips I've shared with you throughout this course.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=103)** Be direct.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=104)** Use the right field types so that your form works well and provides the optimum experience for mobile and desktop users.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=111)** Built a form that looks good.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=113)** Your form should match your company's aesthetics and ensure consistency and promote a polished look.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=119)** Whenever you can, use smart fields.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=122)** Help your user by making it easy.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=124)** Have your form generate city and state automatically from the zip input.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=128)** These types of features speed up the web form completion process and create a seamless user experience.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=134)** Be transparent.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=136)** Explain why you need certain information and what the benefit is to your user from providing it.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=141)** By improving your web form usability and prioritizing the design and context of your form, you'll enhance user experience and get website visitors excited about completing your form and converting.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=154)** I recommend you view my UX for Forms course to learn more about how UX impacts your web form's level of accessibility.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=161)** Again, accessibility refers to how easily your forms can be completed and submitted by many types of people of various backgrounds, and usability refers to how easy someone can accomplish their goal, which in this case means completing a form.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=177)** I hope you've enjoyed this course on building great forms and have learned some new techniques and related work flows.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/building-great-forms-with-html-and-css/next-steps?u=76281980&t=184)** Best of luck to you and happy coding.
